Questioning After the Sudden Death of Zheng Yangchu's Concubine

Fellow Villagers Express Exceptional Grief

To Thoroughly Investigate Whether She Was Forced to Take Poison

Huang, the concubine of the late Zheng Yangchu, a wealthy merchant in the pawnshop industry and a native of Chaozhou, suddenly died suddenly on the night of the 13th of this month. By 8:00 AM the next morning, she was discovered and spread far and wide. Zheng Jiaoshun, Zheng Guoan, Zheng Jinzhi, and other relatives learned of it and reported it to the French police. They all stated that Zheng Huang's death was unclear because the first wife, Zheng Wu, was usually violent and Huang was suspected of being forced to death, requesting a thorough investigation. The police then carried the body to the morgue. The day before yesterday, Wang Ren, prosecutor of the Second Special Court, and Jiang Jun, a forensic doctor, arrived at the morgue at noon to examine the body. Because there were no injuries on the outside, it was impossible to verify the true cause of death. Later in the afternoon, the corpse was dissected, and a small piece of opium that had not completely dissolved was found on the left side of the stomach. All the details have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, the Zheng family prepared a coffin and clothing and went to the morgue to collect the body. At that time, according to a Zheng family member, after the death of her husband Zheng Yangchu, the deceased, although a concubine, was able to abide by the virtues of a woman. Unexpectedly, the first wife Wu was criticized by outsiders, which was despised by the family. This time, the news of Huang's death spread, and fellow villagers expressed exceptional grief. It is also heard that the Chaozhou Fellow Association attaches great importance to this case and intends to request the Second Special Court and the French police to thoroughly investigate whether she was forced to take poison in order to emphasize human life and promote justice.

Husband is Immoral, Commits Crimes, and Has Evidence of Adultery

Young Woman Sues for Divorce

Court Conciliation Fails

Zhang Qinglun, a native of Ningbo, had an affair with Chen Lanfang, a woman from his hometown, in the Republic of China Year 16. He then came to Shanghai to live with her and went through the marriage ceremony, with Shen Zheng as the matchmaker. After the marriage, Zhang did not engage in proper work and associated with bandits. He has been convicted by the government twice. Recently, Chen filed a lawsuit for divorce with the First Special District Court through a lawyer, claiming that Zhang had not engaged in proper work, associated with bandits, neglected her livelihood, and frequently assaulted her. The case was heard yesterday in the 11th Civil Court by Judge Yu Changzi. Chen Lanfang's reasons for divorce were that Zhang did not engage in proper work, associated with bandits, neglected her livelihood, and arbitrarily assaulted her. She also claimed that Zhang was having an affair and had slept with Dai Xiaomei at 46 Chunyang Lane on Dong Youheng Road at 12:00 midnight on the 28th of last month. She reported this to the Jiaxing Road Patrol Room, and Zhang and Dai were arrested. They admitted to having committed adultery twice, which can be verified. However, Zhang stated that he did not want a divorce and denied all the points alleged by the plaintiff. He also accused the plaintiff of having an affair with her cousin-in-law, Lu Weiting, saying that he saw Lu and Chen Lanfang together in the room when he returned home one day, and it was midnight. There was also a landlord who could testify to this. However, Chen Lanfang firmly denied it. The court then summoned Lu Weiting, who denied having an affair with Chen, saying that it was because Zhang borrowed money and failed. The court then advised both parties to reconcile, but ultimately failed because the conditions were too far apart. Finally, Shen Zheng testified about Zhang's beating of Chen Lanfang. The court then issued an order to change the date for further verification.

Zhang Dabao Sentenced for Enticing a Virgin into Prostitution

Sentenced to Four Months Imprisonment with a Two-Year Suspended Sentence

Zhang Hongying, a young woman from Liyang, was seventeen years old and possessed graceful beauty. Due to her family's poverty, on February 28th of this year, her mother brought her to Shanghai and placed her in the care of Zhang Dabao, a woman residing at No. 225 in the Laohuile Lane on Yunnan Road, to work as a maid for a term of three years. However, Zhang Dabao was of questionable character and, seeing the girl's delicate charm, conceived an evil plan. She dressed the girl in seductive attire and took her to the Oriental Hotel to solicit customers. On the 2nd of this month, a client named Yuan Lansheng opened room 252 in the Oriental Hotel and requested Zhang Hongying to stay overnight. That evening, due to a mahjong game with friends that lasted all night, Zhang Hongying managed to preserve her virginity. The next day, Zhang Hongying and Zhang Dabao were spotted on Yunnan Road by Yuan Lansheng, who argued with them to demand the return of his overnight fee.

They were then arrested by police officers and taken to the police station. Zhang Dabao was prosecuted by the First Special Court under Article 249 of the criminal law. The interrogation has concluded, and yesterday morning, presiding judge Feng Shide of the First Criminal Court announced the verdict: Zhang Dabao, with the intention of profit, enticed a respectable woman into indecent acts with others, and is sentenced to four months of imprisonment. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be credited at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. The sentence is suspended for two years. Zhang Hongying was released into the custody of her mother, Tao Zhang. After the pronouncement, Zhang Hongying expressed her unwillingness to return home with her mother. Therefore, the police lawyer Li Zhishan stepped forward and stated that Zhang Hongying feared that if she left, she would be sold as a prostitute by her mother. Thus, she expressed her willingness to continue residing at the Jiliang Institute to receive education, with her mother allowed to visit her from time to time. It is hoped that after receiving adequate education in the future, her mother would take her back. Tao Zhang, on the other hand, requested permission to take her daughter back so that she could explain the situation to her husband. Judge Feng reviewed the statements and instructed Zhang Hongying to remain at the Jiliang Institute temporarily, pending her father's arrival to take her back.

Reading and Answering Questions

More on the Steps of Literary Study, Writing, and Others (2)

Yesterday, we raised three of the most basic questions for studying literature. First, we explained ... (1) What is the literature we need? Today, we will further discuss the second topic. Editor.

(1) How to Read Literary Works? Literary books can be roughly divided into two parts: one part is about theory, and the other part is creation, such as poetry, drama, and novels. The method of reading literary theory books is no different from the method of reading general social science books. We have already had a detailed discussion of this method in the previous issue. Now, we want to talk specifically about the method of reading literary works.

In the eyes of the general public, literature is essentially different from social science. In fact, this is not very accurate. This error arises from regarding literature as entertainment. In essence, literature and social science both express social reality. However, social science is a theoretical dissection, while literature is a depiction of life. The only difference between literature and social science lies in the methods of expression. Social science directly enlightens the reader's intellect; literary works must reach the intellect through the reader's emotions. Reading social science requires a calm mind; reading literary works requires rich emotions. This point should be understood before discussing how to read literary books.

So, how should we read literary books? We can divide it into three steps: first, general reading; second, comparative reading; and third, critical reading.

Let's talk about general reading first. The most common reading method, as we know, is to read each sentence carefully. This is correct. If you don't read classical Chinese works without much content carefully, then you won't be able to learn the only rhetoric, "intonation, rise and fall, pause and break" of the writing. If you don't read science books carefully, then you won't be able to remember the scientific principles you want to remember. However, it would be too clumsy to apply this method to reading literary works. As mentioned earlier, we read literary works not to learn some writing techniques, but to obtain life data. That is to say, we should pay attention to the content of the work. For example, when reading a novel, we should pay attention to how the story unfolds, how the protagonist acts in the story, and what the central problem expressed by the story is. Simply put, just absorb the essence of the story. Even if you forget the other details of the description as you read, it doesn't matter. After reading, if we have a clear impression of the above points, then the preliminary work of our reading is completed. Therefore, reading literary works is not about reading carefully, but about reading a lot. The more you read, the richer the life data will be.

Second, it is comparative reading. It is not enough to simply absorb the content of a work. Because the content of works is diverse, some can nourish our lives, and some can corrode our lives. Therefore, we should filter what we read. This filtering is to compare the living social phenomena with the depictions of the works. We read literary works not only as literary works, but also as social science and as life records. We should not be deceived by the works. We should pay attention to how far the descriptions of the works deviate from reality. For example, there is a novel The Good Earth written by Mrs. Buck of the United States. Many people think that this novel is the best work describing the Chinese countryside. The author meticulously depicts the decline of the Chinese countryside and the famine of the farmers, and attributes the causes of this phenomenon to natural disasters and fate. But if we observe it from reality, are natural disasters the main reason for the decline of the Chinese countryside? Obviously not. The main force that destroys the Chinese countryside is the warlord war and the economic aggression of imperialism. In this way, we can know that this good earth is somewhat distorting the reality, and we have a further understanding of this work. Afterwards, we can talk about critical reading. The so-called critical reading is not to scrutinize every word and sentence of a work, but to criticize the various parts of the work from the development of the entire story and based on one's own sense of feeling. When we read a work, how do we distinguish whether the author's description method is good or not? The description is to make the content more vividly highlighted, and to make the content easier to infect the reader. From this point of view, we know that the detailed description is limited to the reader getting a clearer impression, and enhancing the expression power of the entire content, otherwise it is superfluous. Of course, the most important decision is still in the content of the work, and the form of literature is induced by the content. As in the Good Earth mentioned above, no matter how delicate its description is, but because its content is distorted from reality, whenever the story develops to a higher stage, it deliberately makes it turn or fall, then the description is also a kind of relief, a kind of embellishment and loses its strength.

In addition, I want to talk about one more point, that is, many readers feel difficult to read translated works. This difficulty is of course on the one hand because the descriptions in the translation are very unfamiliar with our real life, and on the other hand, it is because many personal names and place names are not easy to remember. If we want to overcome this difficulty, in addition to using the method of infusing more reading, regarding the former, we can only pay attention to choosing those works that are somewhat related to our lives when choosing works to read, and for the latter, because we only need to absorb the essence of the work, whether personal names and place names can be remembered or not has little to do with our reading.

Spring and Autumn

Exercise

— Yang Yusheng

On the eve of Confucius's great beef feast, there was, as usual, a rehearsal of all sorts of "dances" and "music" related to the ritual. It was said that all educational authorities in areas where there were Confucius temples, and those scholars who were well-known, had to fast and bathe, and participate in the rehearsal.

Indeed, this tune had not been played for a long time, and if not for the rehearsal, there would inevitably be jokes. But jokes still happened, because for this kind of rehearsal, most "literati" were more fearful than excited, so the result of the rehearsal would not be very skilled.

That was the case before. Now, the so-called "dance" and "music" are probably more excited than fearful! So the result will definitely be skillful. However, the general students—perhaps they are also literati—can still strive for perfection, holding the same sex "Die Lü Du" "Du Luo Die" on the not-so-smooth floor in the dormitory and repeatedly "Swinging", it is said that this is also an exercise. From Confucius's point of view, "the younger generation" is indeed "to be feared"!

The Chinese are born lazy and are not willing to act rashly. In order to eat a New Year's beef feast for the Master, they have to brace themselves and rehearse late into the night, which is really rare. In addition, it is said that some people have also used the skill of rehearsal for foreign adults. This is probably the authority that Confucius gave them during the period of riding a raft to float on the sea. As described in the Record of Officialdom Observed, a certain governor of Shandong, in order to entertain foreign adults, had to rehearse all the etiquettes of shaking hands, "yes sir", and other ceremonies, so that he could not close his eyes all night, resulting in "dizziness" and still making many jokes!

This only refers to the rehearsal of "civil affairs". "Those who have civil affairs must have military preparations", now we may as well talk about the rehearsal of military preparations.

It was about the second Jiangzhe War, Sun Chuanfang had already marked the slogan "I will not offend others unless I am offended" on the front, it seemed difficult to break his promise and become the chief of Rong. But cunning has always been a common thing for military strategists. He entrusted the pretext of exercises and viewed the troops at Jianqiao. This exercise, from the Shanghai-Hangzhou line to the "Shanghai-Nanjing line", used "live ammunition shooting", "killing sounds shocking the sky", "spirit doubled". "Suzhou Governor" Yang Yuting was "sent off" when Sun's army was approaching Nanjing. Probably the lineup of Sun's army was far less than the scale of Japan's autumn exercise, so it was not worth a look.

That was still the case before. Now, the call for exercises is overflowing the globe, whether it is the army, the navy, or the air force, no country is willing to lose their opportunity to exercise. This only refers to the exercises of various countries in their own territories, territorial waters, and airspace. However, the US Navy's exercises in the Pacific Ocean have caused fear throughout Japan, which is strictly guarded against. But Japanese troops are exercising everywhere in Chinese territory,

They certainly don't think this is inappropriate, and we Chinese are just turning a blind eye! This kind of "exercise" with a grand spirit is truly "of long standing"! But now the Chinese seem to be "narrow-minded" a lot, knowing to raise a "protest"! Compared to the Qing officials who could not get a stuffy fart out of being beaten three times by foreign adults, it is really enjoyable!

Mirror

— Holding to Buddha

Mirrors are companions to people, especially women, who cannot be without them for a moment. Mirrors are also called "鑑" (jiàn, meaning to examine or reflect), and in ancient times they were made of bronze, but in modern times they began to be made of glass. The Book of Han says, "Use a mirror to examine one's past actions"; "Chen Nu drew with a mirror to observe herself," "Examine the beginning and end, the changes of strength and weakness, and clearly take them as a warning." Sima Guang wrote "Zizhi Tongjian" (Comprehensive Mirror for Aid in Governance), and Zhang Juzheng wrote "Di Jian Tu Shuo" (Illustrated Explanations of Imperial Mirrors), which shows that the function of mirrors is not only to reflect appearances, but also to illuminate the heart.

People have different views on mirrors, some love them, some hate them. For a beautiful woman, as lovely as a flower or jade, she naturally faces the mirror, feeling pity for herself. It's not just that she looks real and lovely in the mirror, making others want to embrace her, but the beauty herself also looks at it again and again, applying rouge and powder, drawing eyebrows and dabbing lips, treating the mirror as a good companion for enhancing her beauty.

In the past, there was a woman who wrote in a poem: "At first sight, I don't know who is facing me, but on closer inspection, I truly feel pity for you." Song Dynasty people also had a few lines of poetry about mirrors, such as "A poor girl, as beautiful as a flower, is only known by the mirror"; "In the mirror, she should know her plain appearance, but in the world, people only see her red makeup"; "She pities herself endlessly, and lingers before leaving." Looking at these few lines of poetry, isn't the mirror a confidant to women? But, I once saw a woman write in a poem: "Looking at my haggard figure over the years, I'm afraid to face the blue mirror and afraid to be seen by others"—when beauty fades, one feels regret, but how can the mirror be held responsible! Ancient people also had a few lines of poetry saying, "The old are unwilling, but what can they do with the mirror"! "Who doesn't cherish a rosy face, but white hair knows it first." "Even if others see it, it's better than seeing it yourself"! Time will not flow backwards, and a rosy face of the past is now white hair, so why resent the mirror.

Grandma Liu mistakenly entered the Grand View Garden and saw an old woman coming towards her, and on closer inspection, it turned out to be herself. Grandma Liu had never seen a large mirror and almost made a joke, which is not surprising. However, this large mirror in the Grand View Garden, which daily reflects the flower-like and jade-like Yingying Yanyan (beautiful women); suddenly reflected an old country woman with wrinkled skin and white hair, is this Grandma Liu's good fortune? Or is it the misfortune of this mirror?

The mirror reflects the shape of things as they are, and has no preconceived notions of beauty, ugliness, length, shortness, squareness, or roundness. A person's heart is like a mirror, if there is no accumulation of dust, and it is diligently wiped every day, it will naturally be bright and clean, without any impurities. It is a pity that people in the world have heavy desires, and their nature is obscured by material desires, isn't it very much like a mirror covered with a thick layer of dust? At this time, if you use this mirror to reflect things, how can you reflect beauty, ugliness, goodness, evil, large, small, square, or round!

The Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Five

Tearful Faces Bid Farewell as People Return Home to Distant Garrisons

Sand and Wind Sweep Through the Night as They Garrison a Lonely City Beyond the Border

The two brothers were also anxious and grabbed two villagers, stomping their feet and telling them not to run. The villagers thought their lives were in danger and squatted on the ground, screaming like pigs being slaughtered. Those villagers who wanted to run away were even more frightened when they saw this and ran even harder. The groom they had just met, carrying a woman with bound feet on his back, supporting her knees with both hands, also flew past. Ziqiang was both annoyed and amused, and said to the two soldiers: "Forget it, let them go, they are too pitiful." The two commoners squatting on the ground kowtowed, broke free from the hands of the two soldiers, and ran away in a puff of smoke. Ziqiang said: "This is terrible, let's go tell the battalion commander." So the four of them walked out of the fort, and the entire team had already arrived at the fort entrance. Ziqiang told the battalion commander about the situation here. Baofang frowned and smiled: "The villagers are pitifully stupid, there's nothing we can do about it. We originally just wanted them to lend us some houses to live in, but since they've all run away, we'll just have to seal up everyone's belongings, we'll live in half and leave half for the people to come back. This time the division commander instructed us again and again to make a good impression, we must make sure our military discipline and conduct are especially good. Everyone suffered a night of hardship, we have no choice, let's temporarily enter the fort to rest." As he spoke, the entire battalion had already entered the fort gate. After busying themselves for half a day, they cleared out twenty households. Soldiers were stationed there. Zhao Ziqiang lived in order of succession, and it happened to be in this mud house with the newly pasted wedding characters. Some simple things in this house had already been moved to the civilian houses where the troops were not stationed before the troops moved in. Now, there is only a mud kang, four yellow mud walls, and two or three pairs of festive couplets pasted on the walls, which cannot be removed. As soon as Ziqiang entered this room, he felt a slight tremor in his heart and stared blankly at the wall. (338)

Research on Inkstones (4)

— A Bored Guest

The culture of an era invariably shifts with the rise and fall of the nation, and all technical crafts advance or decline accordingly. During the Yuan Dynasty, chaos followed chaos, and there was essentially no culture to speak of. At that time, there were only a few inkstone-loving painters, such as Zhao Mengfu and Ni Zan, and the only famous inkstone that was passed down, as seen in the Guangcang Inkstone Record, was that of Empress Wuzong, which need not be discussed in depth. By the Ming Dynasty, culture had developed somewhat again, and special emphasis was placed on the establishment of the painting academy. At that time, scholars and literati, if they entered the painting academy, could immediately increase their reputation. The painting academy during the Xuande period was particularly well-known, and Xie Huan, Shang Xi, Dai Jin, Zhou Wenqing, and others all came from it. Famous painters from Jiangnan, such as Zhou Dongcun, Tang Yin, Qiu Ying, Shen Zhou, Wen Zhengming, Dong Qichang, Chen Jiru, etc., emerged one after another, and the relationship between calligraphy and painting and inkstones became even more crucial. Therefore, all famous calligraphers and painters loved inkstones, and if they obtained a famous stone, they would definitely seek out famous craftsmen to carve it and famous people to inscribe it. When the mines were opened during the Wanli period, Shuiyan (Water Rock) was discovered, and the name of Duan inkstone began to become famous. The Manchu Qing Dynasty succeeded the Ming Dynasty, and because both Kangxi and Qianlong were known for their love of inkstones, they tried their best to collect famous inkstones. Among those seen in the records, there are the twenty-four volumes of the Qianlong Imperial Collection of Western Green Inkstone Records, the sixty-four illustrations of the Baoku Inkstone Records, and six other types of records. Because the times were peaceful and the resources were abundant, the emperor advocated literature and art, and the scholar-officials followed suit. All those who were skilled in poetry and literature, as well as famous artists, devoted themselves to the aestheticization of inkstones, and spared no labor or financial resources to excavate the Duan mines. The essence of Shuiyan was fully expressed, and the beauty of inkstones can be said to have reached its peak, with nothing more to add. According to statistics, during the entire Qing Dynasty,

Famous inkstone lovers included Zhu Yizun, Wang Shizhen, Chen Gongyin, Pan Lei, Shi Runzhang, Wan Sitong, Song Luo, Gao Shiqi, Weng Songnian, Lin Jiren, Huang Shentian, Wang Shu, Ding Jingshen, Shen Tingfang, Ma Riguan, Ma Rilu, Yuan Mei, Wu Shengnian, Liu Yong, Weng Fanggang, Liang Tongshu, Ji Xiaolan, Yuan Shu, Qian Daxin, Ji Shouqiao, Ji Danshi, Wang Wenzhi, Yi Bingshou, Gui Weigu, Chen Hongshou, Wu Lanxiu, Wu Rongguang, Zhang Tingji, Zhang Zhidong, etc.;

Famous inkstone makers included Huang Zongyan, Pan Zihe, Kong Chuanzhuo, Gao Fenghan, Zhang Chun, Wang Yun, Pan Feng, Zhang Chongyi, Wu Yu, Sun Shenfu, Liu Xubai, Zhu Xu, Zhu Long, Gu Erniang, Jin Dongxin, Zhou Lanpo, Yang Longshi, etc.;

Regarding the writings on inkstones, the most famous ones include Gao Guzhai's "Duan Stone Examination," Yu Danxin's "Inkstone Forest," Pan Jiatang's "Duanxi Inkstone Stone Fu and Inscription," Zhu Zhuotuo's "Saying Inkstone and Inkstone Inscription," Shi Yushan's "Inkstone Forest Gleanings," Jin Dongxin's "Inkstone Inscription," Tang Hengquan's "Famous Inkstone Illustration Examination," Yuan Xiangting's "Notes on the Duanxi Inkstone Record in the Pen Record," Lin Peiyun's "Pottery Boat Inkstone History," Ji Xiaolan's "Inkstone Record in the Yuewei Cottage," Gao Fenghan's "Inkstone History," Huang Diancang's "Comprehensive Reference to the Duanxi Inkstone History," Zhu Ertuo's "Short History of Duan Inkstone," Chen Jieting's "Duan Stone Imitation," Ji Shouqiao's "Examination of the Duanxi Inkstone Pits," Wu Shengnian's "Record of the Duanxi Inkstone Pits," Li Zhaoluo's "Record of the Duanxi Inkstone Pits," Wu Lanxiu's "Duanxi Inkstone History," He Shiqing's "Distinguishing Treasures of the Treasure Inkstone Hall," Shen Shiyou's "Inkstone Forest," etc. Others, such as Wang Yuyang, Cao Qiuyue, Gao Xiaoqin, Yang Jingsu, etc., each have many records, which cannot be listed in detail. From this, it can be seen that during the Qing Dynasty, inkstone materials and literature and art both reached their peak, and the changes in inkstones also stopped there.

The Ministry of Education Explains the Examination Issues

The Ministry of Education's explanation of the examination issues is summarized below: (1) For the Shanghai Education Bureau's request for instructions on whether students in this city's middle school examinations who fail one subject can take a supplementary examination on behalf of the education authorities in other cities, the bureau was instructed to allow the bureau to entrust the competent education department to take the supplementary examination on its behalf. (2) The Jiangsu Education Department submitted a request for an explanation of the ambiguity in Article 10 of the Regulations on Graduation Examinations for Middle School Students (this article stipulates that high school students who fail two or one subject are allowed to participate in the examination of each subject in the next session. If they wish to continue their studies, they may be issued a certificate of admission to higher education by the competent administrative agency and be allowed to take the examination for higher education. After being admitted, they will be allowed to be probationary students. They will not be regarded as regular students until they have participated in the examination of each subject in the next session and obtained a graduation certificate. A detailed examination of the provisions seems to have some ambiguity. In case they participate in the examination of each subject in the next session and still fail, those who have not continued their studies will not be allowed to graduate, and those who have continued their studies will not be regarded as regular students, which will greatly hinder the students' future. Can it be allowed to participate in the examination of each subject in the next session once again, in order to provide relief, in accordance with the example of repeating the grade twice?) The department was instructed to allow the student to participate in the examination of each subject in the next session once again, in accordance with the example of repeating the grade twice. (3) The Shanghai National Military Training Committee submitted a request that military training be included in the high school or above school examinations, and the committee was instructed to check that students who fail the military training course will not be allowed to graduate in accordance with Article 6 of the National Education Law, that is, they will not be able to participate in the graduation examination, and that the request to include military training in the school examinations should be unnecessary. (4) The Shandong Education Department submitted two explanatory differences in Articles 62 and 63 of the Middle School Regulations (there are differences in the interpretation of attending the original grade and studying in the original grade in Article 63, and Article 62 does not specify the number of times to repeat the grade). The department was instructed to check that there are no words for repeating the grade in the terms of Article 62 of the Regulations. If a student has been demoted to study in a lower grade for one semester, and still fails two subjects listed in that article next time, they should be ordered to drop out of school. If only one subject fails, or two subjects fail, and the subjects are not as stipulated in that article, they should be handled in accordance with Article 63. As for Article 63, (if they still fail, they should still study in the original grade in the next academic year) has been corrected by the Ministry to (the original grade), and has been notified to all on file.

Inspector of the Ministry of Education, Pang Jingzhou, Criticizes Lu Ping Medical School

The Medical College of Pingda University Is Making Great Progress, While the Equipment of the Lu Medical College Is Simple

Liu Yingshi and Five Others Inspect Various Universities and Colleges in Tianjin

(Special Dispatch from Peiping) Liu Yingshi, Guo Youshou, Sun Guofeng, Chen Kezhong, Zhou Tianfang, and five other inspectors from the Ministry of Education arrived in Tianjin and began to inspect colleges and universities in Tianjin. Pang Jingzhou, a specialist in medical inspection, took the train to Baoding today (15th) at 12:00 noon to inspect the Hebei Provincial Medical College. The Joint Association of Faculty and Staff of National Colleges and Universities in Pingjin decided to entertain the inspectors from the Ministry of Education when they return to Peiping, and to make some suggestions. The details of the situation of each party are recorded as follows:

Mr. Pang Jingzhou's Remarks

Before Mr. Pang left Beiping, a reporter met Mr. Pang in the garden courtyard and inquired about his impressions of inspecting medical education. His reply was as follows: This trip to the north to inspect medical education has been quite pleasant. The Ministry of Education instructed me to inspect medical schools for two reasons: (1) Although some Ministry officials have studied medicine, they are busy with Ministry affairs and cannot leave Nanjing, so I was sent north; (2) Those who run education inevitably have some subjective views when inspecting medical schools. The Ministry of Education asked me to inspect medical schools in North China because of my independent nature. When I left Nanjing, the Ministry did not indicate inspection standards. However, I am responsible for specialized medical inspections. As for the inspection of administrative expenses of various medical schools, Mr. Sun (Guofeng) and Mr. Guo (Youshou) are responsible. Because I have business relationships in Shanghai, I am returning south early. Today, I am going to Baoding to inspect the Hebei Provincial Medical College. I plan to inspect for two days, then go to Kaifeng to inspect the Henan University Medical College for two days, and then take a train from Kaifeng to return south. During this inspection of various medical schools, I deeply felt that medicine is quite necessary in China. Each school has its own advantages and its own unique spirit. The Peiping Union Medical College, a private institution, has the most abundant funding. Although the college was founded by foreigners, it is registered with the Ministry of Education, so it must also be inspected. The National Peiping University Medical College has made rapid progress in recent years. Three years ago, when I traveled to Peiping, I visited the medical college. The situation at that time is still vivid in my mind. This time, each part of the college has made progress, especially the surgery and physical therapy departments. It is a pity that funding is difficult. After the college followed the Ministry of Education's order to change from a four-year system to a six-year system, funding has become even more strained. The Shandong Qilu University Medical College has a long history and complete equipment. The Shandong Provincial Medical College was established a year and a half ago. The school buildings are not sufficient, and the equipment is certainly not as good as that of Qilu University Medical College, but the spirit of hard work is very good. Running a medical school is more difficult than running other schools: (1) Medical schools are the most expensive. Medicine must be practiced, and practice must have affiliated hospitals. All equipment is more complicated than any other school; (2) Medical colleges must be close to society. Some people criticize the quality of medicine not by students' grades but by the simplicity of hospital equipment, because medical schools must have a kind of belief in society. I will return to Shanghai to sort out the report after all medical schools in various places have been inspected, he said.

The Educational Association's Stance

According to Yang Likui, a member of the Peiping-Tianjin University and College Educational Association, the Ministry of Education's dispatch of personnel to the north for inspection prompted some suggestions from the association. The equipment in various northern schools is simple, so it is necessary to suggest to the Ministry of Education to increase funding. Last year, the Ministry of Education merged various colleges and departments of Peiping University, causing disputes because the school was greatly affected. Please ask the Ministry of Education not to implement the merger policy again. The university graduation examination urgently needs to be improved in order to raise the level of various suggestions. When the Ministry of Education's inspection commissioner comes to Beiping again, the Educational Association will hold a meeting to receive him and offer opinions, he said.

Inspecting the Medical College

After Xu Songming, acting president of Peiping University, learned that the Ministry of Education's inspection commissioner was going to the hospital for inspection, he personally greeted them at the hospital at 8:00 a.m. on the 14th. At 8:50 a.m., the Ministry of Education's inspection commissioners Pang Jingzhou, Liu Yingshi, Chen Kezhong, Zhou Tianfang, Sun Guofeng, and Guo Youshou arrived at the medical college and were received by Xu Songming, Dean Wu Xiangfeng, and Secretary Ma Zhidao. They successively visited the basic teaching rooms, including physiology, pathology, anatomy, bacteriology, medicine, chemistry, and physiological chemistry law, eight medical teaching rooms. Next, they went to the affiliated hospital, accompanied by Xu and Wu, and were received by Jian Xianqi, the hospital director. They visited the clinical departments, including internal medicine, surgery, ophthalmology, dermatology, venereology, otolaryngology, pediatrics, obstetrics and gynecology, and physical therapy, eight departments. They also inspected the operating room and wards. Finally, they went to the Second District Health Office for inspection, also accompanied by Xu and Wu, and were received by health teacher Yan Jingqing. The inspectors inquired about the medical college's funding, and Dean Wu Xiangfeng replied that the monthly funding was 19,000 yuan, and the affiliated hospital's funding was more than 2,200 yuan. The inspectors recorded the information they obtained one by one, and left at about 2:00 p.m.

Continuing to Hold the Second Training Class for School Health Personnel

The Municipal Education Bureau Orders the Issuance of Training Methods

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau yesterday ordered the municipal primary and secondary schools in the Wusong District, as well as the registered private primary and secondary schools, saying that a training class for school health personnel had been established and that the bureau had formulated methods. The first session was held in districts such as South Shanghai. This year, after consulting with the Municipal Health Bureau, the second training class for school health personnel will continue to be held in the Wusong District in order to enable teachers and staff of various schools to be familiar with the knowledge and skills of school health, and to fully implement the health subjects prescribed by the curriculum standards issued by the ministry. In addition to formulating the above-mentioned training class methods separately, an examination syllabus is also attached, and all schools are urgently ordered to comply with this order.

Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau and Education Bureau School Health Personnel Training Methods

(1) The purpose of this training class is to train school health administrative personnel and promote the implementation of health courses. (2) This training class will be conducted in districts. The following personnel from municipal primary and secondary schools in the designated districts should attend the lectures, unless there are special circumstances that have been reported to the Education Bureau for approval in advance: (A) the principal (director of the attached primary school) or the director of affairs; (B) the director of training; (C) the physical education teacher; (D) the health teacher. (3) Private registered primary and secondary schools may send one person to attend the lectures at their discretion. (4) This training class will have one director and one deputy director, who will be hired after consultation between the Health Bureau and the Education Bureau. (5) This training class will have a number of lecturers, who will be hired jointly by the Health Bureau and the Education Bureau to be in charge of specialized personnel. (6) The training period and teaching time will be determined by the Health and Education Bureaus in consultation at any time. (7) The location of the training class will be designated by the Education Bureau at any time. (8) Before the start of the training class, each school should separately fill in and report the names, genders, and positions of the personnel attending the lectures (hereinafter referred to as students) to the Education Bureau. (9) When students are absent, the school to which they belong should first explain the reasons to the Education Bureau for leave. (10) In addition to the lecturers assessing the students' academic performance, the Education Bureau may send personnel to investigate at any time. (11) Students who have completed their studies and passed the examination will be jointly issued certificates by the Health and Education Bureaus, but those who have been absent for more than one-quarter of the total study time will not be issued certificates. (12) Students who have not obtained certificates may not serve in educational affairs and positions related to health education.

Shen Bao Radio Weekly

Analysis of AC Radio Power Supply

— Meng Cheng

The most difficult problem to solve in vacuum tube radios is the power supply. DC requires three sets of batteries, A, B, and C. Among them, the A and B batteries are the most problematic. The C battery is easier to solve because of its lower voltage and extremely small current. When using AC, the work assigned to the three sets of batteries will be taken over by two power lines. All power is taken from the power lines.

The AC radio power supply can be divided into four parts to explain:

(1) Power Transformer Ordinary power supplies are composed of two or more transformers. One transformer lowers the AC voltage of 220 or 110 volts on the power line to an appropriate filament voltage and directly connects it to the filament or hot wire on the vacuum tube to replace the A battery in a DC radio. Another transformer raises or lowers the voltage from the power line to the maximum required plate voltage. However, the voltage coming out of the transformer is AC voltage, and the B and C batteries in the radio must be DC voltage, so other components must be connected to convert this AC voltage into DC voltage.

(2) Rectifier A rectifier has unidirectional conductivity, meaning that current can only flow in one direction inside the rectifier and cannot flow in the opposite direction. Therefore, the function of the rectifier is to cut off half of the positive and negative time-varying AC voltage and convert it into a unidirectional pulsating voltage. There are many types of rectifiers. In radios, the most common is the application of diode vacuum tubes. There are so-called mercury rectifier tubes, which are also a type of diode, but a small amount of mercury is placed in them during manufacturing to increase the rectification efficiency. In high-power dynamic speakers, a low DC voltage must also be applied to increase its output power. This low DC voltage now uses a new type of copper oxide rectifier to take power directly from the AC voltage.

(3) Filter The plate and grid voltages required in radios are all fixed DC voltages. The pulsating voltage coming out of the rectifier, although DC, changes in voltage from time to time, gradually increasing from zero to the maximum and then gradually decreasing from the maximum to zero. Therefore, it is necessary to modify the pulsating voltage to a fixed voltage. The function of the filter is to reduce the range of the pulsating voltage to a minimum. The voltage coming out of the filter is almost fixed. The filter is composed of several fixed capacitors and several iron-core coils. The capacitor has a large capacitance and the ability to store electrons. When the voltage is extremely high, it temporarily stores the current, but when the voltage decreases, the current can still flow out. In this way, it can make up for the deficiency and reduce the voltage pulsation. The iron-core coil has a large self-inductance and opposes changes in current when the voltage increases or decreases. In other words, the iron-core coil also has the effect of maintaining a fixed voltage. (To be continued)

The Structure and Principles of ABC Battery Eliminators

— Li Yuanqing

The power sources used in old-fashioned radios are mostly supplied by dry cells or storage batteries. Such power sources are neither convenient to carry nor easy to manage. New-style radios, with the addition of only a rectifier tube and a few small parts, can have an inexhaustible power supply. The recent popularization of wireless radios among the general public in China is truly due to the contribution of ABC battery eliminators (ELIMINATOR).

The structure and principles of commonly used ABC battery eliminators are as follows:

A-Battery Section

Because the use of the A-battery is only to heat the filament and emit electrons, both AC and DC power can be used. The A-battery commonly used in AC radios uses a transformer to reduce the external voltage (110 or 220V) before use. As shown in the figure, S1 is a 2.5V secondary coil, used to burn the filaments of the detector and amplifier tubes. S3 is the secondary coil of V5, dedicated to the filament of the rectifier tube. R is a 20-ohm center-tapped resistor (which must be directly connected to the tube socket when in use; please refer to issue 11 of this publication). Its function is to obtain a point where the filament potential value remains constant. The screen grid circuit (i.e., B and C-) is connected to this point to reduce AC hum. If you want to reduce AC hum to the minimum, then except for the final stage power output tube, it is best to use indirectly heated vacuum tubes for all the rest (INDIRECT HEATER TUBE).

B-Battery Section

The B-battery is applied to the plate and screen grid of the vacuum tube to absorb the electrons emitted from the filament. Because electrons are negatively charged, the plate and screen grid must be connected to a positive voltage to be effective. Also, because any change in the plate voltage can easily cause noise, the B-battery must use stable DC voltage.

Although the structure of B-battery eliminators varies, their principles are always based on the following four points:

(1) The plate voltage of new-style radios is as high as 250 volts or more. Therefore, the external voltage of 110 or 220 volts seems too low. Therefore, the first step is to increase the external voltage to the required value before it can be used. The transformer T and its secondary coil S2 are responsible for this mission (see figures A and B).

(2) The rectifier tube V1 uses the principle of like charges repel and opposite charges attract to convert the increased B voltage into a unidirectional pulsating current (as shown in figure C). This pulsating DC current cannot be directly applied to the plates of each vacuum tube for the time being, otherwise the loudspeaker will emit extremely loud buzzing noise, disrupting the correct sound.

(3) The function of the filter is to convert the rectified pulsating current into a smooth DC current. We know that the choke coil has a very large magnetic inductance (commonly 30 Henrys. If there is an electric loudspeaker, its magnetic field coil can be used as a choke coil).

Therefore, it is very difficult for it to pass pulsating current. However, the function of the capacitor is the opposite. The fluctuating pulsating current, since there is no way to go for the time being, can only rest in the capacitor for a while before slowly passing through the choke coil. As a result, a stable DC current can be obtained at point D.

(4) If only one type of B voltage is needed in the radio, then the work of the B-battery eliminator can end here. But in fact, the radio must have various different B voltages in order to supply the detector, oscillator, and amplifier tubes. Therefore, it must go through a voltage dividing procedure before it can be completed.

Various B voltages of different levels are reduced by using resistors connected in series in the plate circuit. As shown in the figure, if the amplifier tube V5 needs a plate voltage of 180V, according to Ohm's law, RI = ohm. Also, if the detector tube V2 needs a plate voltage of 45V, we get

ohm

C-Battery Section

The C-battery is connected to the grid of the amplifier tube to prevent distortion during amplification. What is needed is a negative voltage with a constant value. Usually, a section of resistor is used to connect between the filament center-tap resistor (or cathode) and B- to complete the circuit. As shown in the figure, V4 is a type 47 pentode amplifier tube. When the plate voltage is 250V, the required C voltage is -6.5V. According to Ohm's law, we get R = 450 ohms. Similarly, we get R3 = = 2700 ohms. Those connected in parallel with R3 and R4 are IMF fixed capacitors, whose function is to allow low-frequency current to pass easily and improve the sound quality of vacuum tube amplification.

Various Rectifier Tubes

— Yizhi

Since the prevalence of AC radios, rectifier tubes have replaced the work of B and C batteries, supplying plate and grid voltages. The rectifier tube is originally a diode, using the "Edison effect" to convert AC power into half-wave or full-wave DC power. Connected with resistors to adjust the appropriate voltage, it is applied to the radio. Compared with using batteries, the procedure is convenient and economical. Therefore, rectifier tubes can be improved and evolved with the needs of the times along with other types of vacuum tubes in radios. Now, I will briefly describe the characteristics and effects of various types.

The 80 full-wave rectifier tube used to be the most suitable rectifier tube. It is very suitable for supplying power to four-tube or seven-tube radios. It can also be used for half-wave rectification. When using it, connect the two plates in parallel, then the output current can be slightly increased compared to when doing full-wave rectification. The characteristics of this tube are: filament voltage is 5 volts, filament current is 2 amps, plate voltage is 350-550 volts, plate current is 125-135 milliamps.

The 81 half-wave rectifier tube has a filament voltage of 7.5 volts, a filament current of 1.25 amps, a plate voltage of 700 volts, and a plate current of 85 milliamps. Because the output voltage of this rectifier tube is very high, the filter setting is slightly more expensive, and it is rarely used in ordinary radios. If two of these tubes are used, they can be used for full-wave rectification (the wiring diagram is simplified due to space limitations).

82 full-wave mercury vapor rectifier (FULL WAVE MERCURY VAPOR RECTIFIER) is an advanced micro-quantity of mercury. When in use, the mercury is evaporated, and the tube is filled with mercury atoms. Ions with positive charges neutralize the negative electrons repelled between the filament and the plate, so as to increase the total number of electrons and strengthen the rectification effect. The voltage drop in this type of rectifier tube is only 15 volts. When using this tube, each of the two plates must be connected in series with a high-frequency choke coil, and the tube should be isolated with a nickel cover to avoid chaotic AC noise caused by rectification changes on the radio, and can increase its sensitivity. Because the internal resistance of this tube is very low, special attention must be paid when using it to prevent its load from exceeding 50%, otherwise the filament will be easily damaged. The characteristics of this tube are: filament voltage is 2.5 volts, filament current is 3 amps, plate voltage is 500 volts, and plate current is 125 milliamps. This tube is commonly used in new-style radios.

83.523. The characteristics and effects of the full-wave mercury vapor rectifier tube are almost the same as those of the 82 tube, but the filament voltage is 5 volts and the plate current is 500 milliamps, which is twice that of the 82 tube. In today's seven-tube radios and above, it should replace the 8081 tube.

84 indirectly heated full-wave rectifier tube. This tube is specially used in car radios. The filament power supply can be DC or AC. Its characteristics are: filament voltage is 6.3 volts, filament current is 0.5 amps, plate voltage is 225 volts, and plate current is 50 milliamps.

2525 indirectly heated voltage doubler rectifier tube. This tube is specifically used for AC/DC dual-purpose radios or transformerless radios. There are two ways to connect it. If the radio is for both AC and DC, it can be connected in a half-wave mode; if it is only used for AC, it can be connected to a voltage doubler. In other words, it converts AC voltage into twice the DC voltage. The principle and connection method for its voltage doubler function will be described later when there is time. For the characteristics of this tube, please refer to my article "Introduction to the 25Z5 New Vacuum Tube", published in issue 23 of this publication. This tube is widely used and is used as a rectifier in today's AC/DC dual-purpose radios.

12Z3 indirectly heated half-wave rectifier tube. The filament voltage is 12.6 volts, the filament current is 3 amps, the plate voltage is 230 volts, and the plate current is 60 milliamps. This tube is also commonly used in AC/DC dual-purpose radios.

Free Talk ]

Further Discussion on the Beijing School, the Shanghai School, and Others

— Gu Ming

Some time ago, when the "Beijing-Shanghai" issue was most discussed, I briefly discussed the lack of good literary works, and thus thought of the increasingly deteriorating and difficult material environment, where there are no talents of any kind, not only literary ones. However, the South, due to the natural environment, still has a few people who are writing, etc. At the same time, a certain gentleman strongly opposed this, thinking that literature has nothing to do with nature, and that Russia, despite its extremely difficult material environment, still had Pushkin, etc. That theory is also very valuable, because in our current situation, Pushkin should emerge even more, which can be a stepping stone for modern writers to encourage themselves. That's right. But all geniuses, celestial beings, talents, ghosts, whether literary, philosophical, natural scientific, or social scientific, must be found among humanity. Since they are in this society, they must be dominated by the material environment, which is also knowable. Have you ever seen an uneducated rickshaw puller write poetry, or someone who doesn't know English read Shakespeare's original works? There's no way to imagine it, that's the fact. Pushkin had to understand Russian first to write poetry; he also had a melancholy dark night and a vast sky on his head, which were imprinted in his poems—it's really not a strange reason.

The Eastern Victory Divine Continent has become more and more "barren and poor" recently, which is also a fact. "Abundant products" and "fertile land" have long become deceptive and self-deceptive talk. To grow peonies in rubble, to pick big Sterculia monosperma fruits in the weeds, is also an impossible fact except with the magic of Brahmins. A certain gentleman hopes that Pushkin will emerge from this, which is well-intentioned, but if there were geniuses like Pushkin, whether a hundred or a thousand, they might have already turned into something else due to the harsh environment.

The lack of genius, the scarcity of works, both spirit and material have become complete poverty. A few small soldiers and petty thieves are wildly praising and cheering in the literary world, greatly dividing it into "Beijing" and "Shanghai." Unable to name it, I name it "wild fox Zen." It is knowable how ridiculous the theory is when a wild fox talks about Zen principles. If one's ambition is a small chicken or a wild rabbit, and one declares "I am a vegetarian" or "I am frank," how much worse is that! Many people want to get rich and live forever in the literary world, which is no different from this. There are more foxes but fewer Zen foxes in the North, and fewer foxes but more Zen foxes in the South. Just looking at those people talking about the classification of literature or the methods of writing poetry, with the audience all being young people, one can vaguely see one or two aspects of fox Zen. —

Strolling Through the Confucian Temple (Continued)

— Bai Ge

The Dacheng Hall is already very old, and everything shows a haggard and trembling appearance, only the ten dragon pillars in front are particularly majestic and moving. It is said that these dragon pillars are among the first or second best in China, and they have a very important place in the history of Chinese stone carvings. I don't understand art, but when I see them, I just want to spiral up to them and shout three times. Modern gold-worshipping art has suffocated us so much that we can't even breathe! In front is a plaza paved with bricks and tiles. Those bricks and tiles, as long as you peck them with something, the pecked area will be soaked. It is said that they are from the Han Dynasty, so they are called Han bricks. But one thing is laughable, that is, the person leading the way must enthusiastically explain to you that the bricks and tiles sweat, so they are called sweating bricks. This is only for geologists to study, it's none of our business. Inside the hall, naturally sitting in the center is Confucius, and on both sides are the Four Associates and the Ten Philosophers as usual. The scepter held by Confucius is really unsuitable. It is said that it was originally made of green jade, but later the Confucius Mansion replaced it with the current one, fearing that it would be stolen. Turning out to the left, there are a few stone railings that can provide us with a little legend. Once Qianlong came here, patted these railings with his hand, and they made a clanging sound. When he reached the third one, Qianlong told a joke, "Dare you ring again," so the following ones didn't ring. Although this is a laughable legend, it is indeed more interesting to go and pat those railings after knowing this legend. Every time I pass by there, I have to pat them a few times.

Behind it is the Sleeping Hall, which is brilliant and dazzling, and all the steps, walls, tiles, and stones are brand new, unlike the dilapidated scene of the Dacheng Hall.

Xiang Lake in Xiaoshan

— Tang Kun

Once across the Qiantang River, the first county is Xiaoshan; in the west gate of this county, there is Xiang Lake. Although it is not as famous at home and abroad as West Lake, some places are more lovable than West Lake.

Xiang Lake is not like West Lake's "gaudy and heavily adorned," she has a simple and ancient style. We can say that West Lake is a charming noblewoman, while Xiang Lake is a graceful village girl. In West Lake, at a glance, it is all red and green colors, which makes people feel too vulgar; as for Xiang Lake? At a glance, in spring and summer, it is an endless expanse of water, with rippling tiny waves, and the banks are lush with leaves, dense shadows, reflected in the lake, as if constantly following the circles of water patterns spreading out, but in fact they are still. Among the green leaves, some bamboo fences and thatched cottages are occasionally revealed, and sometimes a long cock-a-doodle-doo or a dog bark is heard. Suddenly, a woman fetching water runs to the lakeside to fetch water, and the calm lake surface is broken. Deep in the misty waves, there may be a simple little boat, floating lonely. In autumn and winter, the lake changes into a clear and pale garment. The lake shore is full of sparse branches, leaving no dead leaves. Girls blowing water caltrop reeds glide in small boats, singing tunes in the lake casually. Most of the people living by the lake make a living by burning kilns. Every time the sun sets in the west, wisps of kiln smoke sway in the air, and the wild birds flying up and down in the lake become the best scenery in the lake. The left bank of the lake is a high and low mountain peak, with white clouds undulating, which makes people imagine. In the middle of the lake, several small islets protrude from the water surface; with miscellaneous trees and a residence for one or two water birds on them. Dingshan Mountain, Yilan Pavilion, Yahu Mountain, etc., are all secluded scenic spots in the lake. The campus of the Xiang Lake Rural Normal School of Zhejiang Province is built on Dingshan Mountain, surrounded by ten thousand bamboos, making it even more majestic and quiet. It is truly the most beautiful place in Xiang Lake. In recent years, people who admire the name of Xiang Lake and come from afar to visit are more and more every day. In the near future, Xiang Lake may become as famous as West Lake.

The Old Village Warden

— Huanming

That white-haired, trembling-lipped old village warden was the first visitor I saw after I got home. He walked into the door very humbly, opened his inkstone on the table in the hall, and lifted his pen, shaking it on a gray-white piece of paper...

"What... what is your name, how old are you?"

"Okay, okay, Afa, I see you coming to investigate the household registration all day long," my mother said, "Investigating the household registration all day long, it's really ghostly. I haven't seen a report on the population statistics in the county. You just write some names and ages, seventy or eighty, on your own." "Oh, oh, yes, yes, Madam," he scribbled a name on that "Household Registration Inspection License": "I'll stick it on the door for you, I..."

After sticking it on, he took a small fee and left. Not even half a month after living there, the old village warden came again. He was humming, his eyes were dull, he was leaning on a door bolt with his right hand, and his face was very ugly - he was sick. The things he brought were still the same as last time, inkstone, pen, a roll of household registration inspection license paper. He opened the inkstone uneasily, shaking his hands: "What... what is your name, how old are you?"

"Are you going to inspect the household registration again? This... is really serious, too serious, isn't it?"

"This is the order from "above"... "Above" ordered us to inspect like this..."

"Is there an official document? - This handling fee is too unreasonable!"

He uneasily, barely smiling, mumbled; "Didn't bring it - forgot to bring it..."

"I have been abroad for many years, and I have never encountered this kind of serious investigation - even foreign countries don't have it, and they don't need handling fees..." I said suddenly... "This is your village warden's "extra income," isn't it!"

His eyes showed a pitiful light... " - Don't call me village warden, I am a village policeman. Yes, yes, the village policeman is the village warden... Hahaha..."

"Is it "extra income?"" I asked closely.

He was embarrassed and coughed for a while, trembling his lips... "To tell you the truth, the village policeman has no salary, right? Hahaha - The amount is limited, you, rich people, don't care, hahaha!"

After taking the money, he picked up the inkstone and wanted to leave. He paused and said... "Thank you, we "haven't" people really have no way, we're old, a "bachelor," and when we're sick, we have to ask you to help, without support - to tell you the truth, the village policeman has no salary."

The day before New Year's Eve, I had to leave home. Following my luggage out the door, I found the old village warden leaning on the door bolt and walking up the threshold of my house again. The things he brought were still the same as last time, inkstone, pen, that roll of gray-white paper, probably still the household registration inspection license paper, right?

About "The Sinister Black Hand"

— Mu Mutian

Ke Jia's "The Sinister Black Hand" was published in the New Year's issue of "Literature." It is a relatively long poem. Compared with the poems in "Brand," it is a big step forward.

From this poem, it seems that Zang Kejia is gradually trying to get rid of his "small self" and striving to shift from personal description to social description, to find the themes of his poems from the larger society.

In "The Sinister Black Hand," Zang Kejia describes the shield and spear contained in the construction of the church in the city. His purpose is to expose the sins of the church. He noticed the two aspects: the situation of the churchgoers who come to worship and the situation of the coolies who built the church. In one place, under the rule of one God, there are two different worlds. Being both "sons of God," why are some people like this and some people like that? So, in the end, he imagined the rebellion of the slaves and predicted that "then this church will become their dining room or bedroom." Here is revealed the demand of the liberals, revealing the anti-religious sentiment. He can expose the point that the great powers invaded China by using religion as a weapon to anesthetize the Chinese people ( ) This is indeed worthy of our attention.

Religion, this thing, really does not know how much sin it has created. Thinking of the situation of the church in Europe in the Middle Ages, one can only add the words "unspeakable" to its sins. The work of progressive people for hundreds of years has failed to drive it out of European society, and when it comes to the time of competing for colonies, the invaders use religion to give the untouchables anesthetic injections. On this land of China, how many countless sins has it committed! Think about the situation before the "Boxer Rebellion," which would make one's hair stand on end. Since the May Fourth Movement, the anti-religious movement has flourished for a few years, but now this movement seems to be "sluggish." It seems that everyone is looking at the big picture, and few people are willing to start with the small things. Zang Kejia can catch this topic of religious aggression, even if the expression is not enough, it is worth recommending.

This relatively large theme made him adopt the form of a long poem. It made him quite abandon his narrow philosophy. This is a more advanced place than the poems in "Brand." Later, if he further recognizes the society, he will naturally not be wrong. And this method of seeking great materials in ordinary real life, I think, is also what other poets should learn. (To be continued)

A Tentative Translation of the Book of Songs

— Yu Shixia

There is a Fox

(1)

There is a lonely fox, on the stone bridge of that Qi River. I can't help but worry for him in my heart, that man has no trousers on!

(2)

There is a lonely fox, at the ferry of that Qi River. I can't help but worry for him in my heart, that man has no belt either!

(3)

There is a lonely fox, beside that Qi River. I can't help but worry for him in my heart, that man has no clothes to wear!

Dusk (7)

— Jin Yi

The scenery in the moonlight is solemn, and they sit there peacefully, breathing the fresh air. Suddenly, there was the sound of an iron gate being opened, the car horn broke the silence, and the dogs were barking noisily. All this made their brains feel painful like poison, and Qingzhi immediately stood up and closed the window.

"It's probably another banquet."

"Who knows, it's always these annoying things!"

After they said these two sentences, they fell silent again, only the pendulum of the wall clock was ringing evenly.

The door was suddenly pushed open, and the maid's voice was saying...

"Are the young ladies in the room? Why are you sitting in the dark? Do you know, the third young lady is back."

"Is she back from Nanjing? She didn't even write a letter."

"That's it, and she brought two children with her."

"Oh, then let's go downstairs to see her." Qingsong said to Qingzhi.

"No need, the third young lady said she'll come to see you later."

"Then turn on the lights first."

The lights were on, they stood up, straightened their crumpled clothes, and ordered the maid to make some light tea.

After a burst of messy, fine footsteps, Qingbai led in six-year-old Lingling and four-year-old Luer.

"Hello, sisters. Stand still and bow to your aunts." Qingbai ordered the two children after bowing to them. The well-behaved children didn't have any shyness and did as she said generously.

They had already stood up, showing long-unseen smiles to welcome them, and walked over happily to shake the children's hands.

"Hello, you, when did you arrive?"

"I just came after getting off the train," Qingbai was still so lively, letting go of one hand holding the children, and brushing her hair, "Sisters, please sit down."

"Then let's all sit down."

Qingbai was wearing a purple dress, tailored very fashionably. Although she had given birth to two children, she still had a very slender figure. Her face was painted with rouge and powder. Although it was said that she was already twenty-eight years old, she looked only about twenty-three or twenty-four years old.

"This time, what made you think of coming back?"

"If it were up to him, he probably wouldn't want me to come back in this lifetime," Qingbai showed a little happy sigh, "It just so happened that he was going to Yunnan for business, so naturally I couldn't follow him, so I took this opportunity to come back."

"In the blink of an eye, we haven't seen each other for five years!"

Securities Shorts' Walls Shake, Bond Market Opens Up from Dullness

New High Prices Are Found for 19 Shan and Others

Yesterday, the market of the Chinese Securities Exchange gradually fluctuated. After more than ten days of hovering and brewing, the dull and stagnant situation suddenly opened up, and there was a feeling of sudden enlightenment. The multi-party and short-party have been in a stalemate for a long time, and at this time, the short-party's walls suddenly shook. It is because the March futures are getting closer to delivery, and the large number of floating shorts have to be closed early to avoid the pain of temporary squeeze. Judging from its past trends, although the hovering date is long, the market price has not fallen, and the bulls have a clear advantage. Therefore, although there is no favorable news for the bulls in the environment, the shorts are forced to drop the period due to the relationship between the supply and demand of chips, which makes the market price see new high prices from the extremely dull situation. In the first two rounds of the morning, the situation was extremely strong, and No. 5 and No. 59 were bought very enthusiastically. Although No. 16 was sold, it was still seen that demand exceeded supply, so each round had an increase of 5 fen to 2 jiao. Although the number is small, the trend is consistent. Alert retail short-sellers rushed to make up again in the afternoon, and No. 17 was also bought quite enthusiastically. The drop-in transactions of various gangs were also quite lively, so the rising trend did not weaken in the afternoon, and each round continued to rise by 3, 4, and 5 jiao. However, the closing price of the 22-year customs was only 1 or 2 jiao smaller, which is also irrelevant to the overall difference. In total, 19 Shan, 20 Volume 20 Customs, and Unified Salt Tax all found new high prices. The salt tax of 53 yuan has been hovering for more than ten times, and those who failed to break through are now seeing a breakthrough. The popularity has suddenly increased, and the future may continue to rise. The market price result is an increase of 2, 3 jiao to 6, 7 jiao. The total transaction fee is 11,206,200 yuan, including 6,200 yuan for spot and 11,200,000 yuan for futures. New York Silver Mine Stocks Plunge Fiercely

Xinfeng Foreign Firm reported on the 15th that the New York stock market plunged fiercely in silver mine and other stocks due to Treasury Secretary Morgenthau's opposition to the current actions on silver. The silver price once fell by 2 points, and the huge plunge created a new record for this year. United States Metallurgical (silver stock leader) plummeted 9 yuan, and all stocks were affected and fell unanimously. In the end, the government proposed to allow Cuba to import liquor without restrictions, and the market recovered slightly due to the relationship between multi-party and short-party chips. In the small exchange, mine stocks fell out, power plant stocks were settled, the market was also tired, and bonds were mixed. Highly speculative bonds had been rising for several days, and the bulls came out very enthusiastically. The total transaction volume for the day was 1.34 million shares. (Wheat) The bulls slightly sold, and the spot demand was very good. The weather in the wheat producing area was too early. (Cotton) The Treasury Department's opposition to silver legislation caused the inflationists to be very frustrated. The朋克海案 (Pengke Hai Case) may be passed in the House of Representatives tomorrow and then sent to the Senate. Grain, Flour, and Wheat Sales Extremely Weak

Yesterday, the flour market opened in the morning with prices initially flat, then stabilizing. The quoted price for foreign wheat was around 45 cents in Chicago and 10 cents in Canada. After the opening, sentiment was generally flat, and actual sales remained weak, with purchasing power being the weakest seen since the market opened. However, factories held firm, and short covering pushed prices slightly higher, improving market sentiment. By the afternoon opening, trading was quiet, but due to more shorts in the market, prices rose slightly, improving sentiment. However, actual sales remained unchanged, ultimately feeling firm but with some slackness. As a result, the current month rose by 7.5 li, April rose by 5 li, May rose by 2.5 li, June rose by 1 fen, and July and August each rose by 2.5 li.

Yesterday, there was very little trading of standard wheat futures. Only one transaction was opened for March, April, June, July, and August in both the morning and afternoon sessions. The market was very quiet, and there were no spot wheat transactions. Soochow glutinous rice rose slightly by 5 fen.

—Suddenly a Turnaround in Late Rice Market—

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, over thirty sources (more than 5,000 piculs) arrived, mostly late rice, with a small amount of thick glutinous rice. Although North and South shipping companies continued to purchase late rice, the volume was not as strong as in the previous market. A total of over 2,000 bags of Qingjiao, Songza, Xilian late rice were received. The market situation did not show much change. However, various types of thick glutinous rice saw a sudden revival in urban and rural shops, a trend that had been somewhat lackluster since the initial market. Ultimately, after a long period of weakness, it was difficult to immediately achieve a strong performance. Therefore, the price of glutinous rice from Changbang, Soochow, Nangang, etc., only increased slightly by 5 fen. The supply and demand for Duyang pointed rice remained peaceful, with little change in market conditions. Yuan-converted goods lacked flavor and were relatively strong. The supply of Yin Yuan was slightly higher, but the sales were average, showing a slightly soft trend.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, 27 or 28 shipments of various goods arrived from the lower reaches of the river. The sales of various colors continued to improve in the market. White glutinous rice, early thin rice, Yangshe pointed rice, and Yin Yuan and Yuan rice all showed a firm trend.

No Telegrams Sent for Silk, Tea, and Chinese Silk

The current price of silk in New York has fallen to $450, and the price of Japanese silk in Yokohama is only $470-480. As a result, the market price of Chinese silk has also fallen. Various manufacturers in Shanghai believe that the cost of B-grade white factory silk is $700-800 per bale, resulting in significant losses. No silk telegrams were sent, and there were no transactions of current silk. Market sentiment continued to be sluggish.

Qimen Tea Industry Remains Active

The black tea produced in Qimen, Fuliang, Jiande, and other places amounts to no less than 60,000-70,000 chests each year. Last year, there were about 300 tea processing firms. The business results showed that most of them suffered losses. As a result, no less than 20-30 firms were forced to close down. The tea season is about to begin, and various firms in Qimen and Fuliang are actively preparing for their operations. They have been in contact with various tea warehouses in Shanghai for loans, and the situation remains active.
