Shen Bao Local Supplement

Informal Talk

The Marriage System Under Feudal Remnants

—Jia Wei

Recently, my friend He Jun mentioned that Lin Jun had been looking depressed and unhappy lately. The reason, he said, was that his parents had already set the date for his wedding. I remember back in the autumn of last year! I heard that Lin Jun had already been "betrothed" by his parents' arrangement. But at that time, I didn't hear him say that he was unwilling. But this time, I heard that he was against his "parents' orders," and had already explained and argued with them several times.

Yes, Lin Jun is very young—just turned twenty—and is still a high school student and not yet "self-reliant." If he is going to talk about marriage so soon (although he doesn't have to bear the burden at this time), then whether we say it subjectively or objectively, it is still too early! But since Lin Jun is under his parents' financial control, and I heard that his parents' intentions are very firm this time, therefore, although Lin Jun is resolutely resisting, what the outcome will be is difficult to predict—Lin Jun is also very passive. Comedy or tragedy? It is difficult to "resolve" what will happen "next time"!

Originally, in the case of ordinary "rich kids, even though they are still immature, not fully developed, and have no skills," they are still able to get a "good wife" to accompany them—what is called a "virtuous mother and good wife." In 19th-century society, such pathetic and laughable facts were very common. But in this day and age—although "free love" and "marriage autonomy" are being loudly proclaimed everywhere, marriages conducted through deceitful and hypocritical "matchmakers' words" are still prevalent. These "profit-seeking" "matchmakers" have harmed countless young men and women and created countless "single men and resentful women," but why are they still rampant everywhere? The reason, generally speaking, is!

The hateful and detestable poison of feudal remnants is deeply hidden in the stubborn and outdated minds of ordinary people with "a little property" or more. The reason why people with sons are eager to arrange marriages for their sons is because they have "money"; they don't have to worry about "eating" or "clothing," and all they have in mind is "eagerly awaiting grandchildren." What they want is "good reputation": they are waiting day and night to be called "blessed with many children and long life" by their "comrades"—those who "share the same ideals"! In this way, they can gain the praise and envy of their "comrades," and also achieve "carrying on the family line" and "honoring their ancestors."

As for those who have daughters, what they have in mind is...since daughters will eventually become "someone else's" one day, then why bother spending more money on "raising" them—of course, there are also those who pamper their "precious daughters," but that is an exception. Therefore, once they reach a "certain" age—mostly "early marriage," right?—they are always planning to marry them off to "someone else"—to "sell" them. Look—both parties are under these conditions; and they are unwilling and don't need to consult their children's aspirations, future prospects, and lifelong happiness, because they know that this is "predestined" and can be determined by their "fate," right?!

Okay, all they need to do is wait for the "matchmakers" to come and turn things upside down and bring the two parties together, making this "transaction." After explaining how "well-matched" the two families are (?), then all they need to do is have the family fortune tellers "arrange" the children's "eight characters"; and based on what these "omniscient immortals" say about "harmony" or "conflict," they decide the children's "lifelong affairs." And society probably adds a lot of excitement because of their "fate's decision"—"comedies of happiness," "comedies of sorrow," please pay attention to the "social news" columns of major newspapers!

Unfortunately, in today's social organization, all the contradictions are becoming more and more acute day by day...The impact of the global economic panic, the wave of collapse of the agricultural economy, has flooded every city with an increasing number of unemployed people; ordinary unfortunate people are all falling into this vortex, frantically crushing and toppling each other in a final struggle. And pitiful are those young people who grow up in families poisoned by feudal remnants, who do not yet have the ability to be independent—there are many who have considerable ability and knowledge but cannot find a way out—and yet are destined to shoulder a "virtuous mother and good wife" and "carry on the family line"—which of course is not "economically independent"—and must bear the great burden of "many children and grandchildren." And the facts will tell us what their future will be like!

Young friends with aspirations! To liberate yourselves from the "shackles of the old ethics" and seize true "freedom," the only way is to work hard to eradicate and annihilate these feudal remnants; but if you want to obtain the true meaning of "free love," you can only find it in the "social organization" that will be reformed in the future.

Regret

—Lingzi

—A Preliminary Attempt at Psychological Sketch—

When he told me that he agreed to what I said... "From now on, we'll just be friends," although my lips were moving and uttered this sentence... "You also know that if you don't agree with me, we won't even be friends in the future"; but my heart, in my heart, felt like it had been electrocuted, shocked and regretful. After I introduced Fen to him and heard him say that Fen expressed her love for him, I not only regretted not letting him love Fen, but also hated myself and hated him.

Today is Sunday, I went to his place, and the maid said that he went out with a young lady. This sentence was like a sharp knife stabbing into my heart, turning regret into hatred, and an inexplicable jealousy filled my mind. I don't hate him, I hate Fen. I deeply feel that... Fen, she is my rival in love! I sat in his study for an hour or two. I didn't want to rummage through his drawers, but I was so bored that I wanted to do something, and I hated Fen, and a surge of jealousy stirred my nerves, wanting to find the letters Fen gave him to read. Unexpectedly, I rummaged through his drawers, and Fen's letters were nowhere to be found (probably hidden on his person), but I found the letter I gave him the day before yesterday, arranging to see him today. It would have been better if I hadn't looked at it, but the more I looked at it, the more I hated it, and I tore it into pieces at will. He said we were friends. Can a friend's appointment be broken? - However, a lover is closer than a friend, Fen came, how could I not let him go out with Fen and stay at home to wait for me? Thinking of this, I hate Fen, and at the same time hate myself... Fen took him away from my arms, hateful, but I myself didn't tell him that I couldn't love him and taught him to love others and just be friends, how could Fen have taken him away? I should blame myself, why is it that I still love him in my heart, but I don't want to love him because of some future?

There was a dish of sweets on his table, Magpie Kele Sakura Candy, etc., silver paper, green paper, red paper, white paper, colorful, really cute. I ate a few pieces casually, looked out the window, and the spring rain was falling in wisps. I was wondering when I suddenly thought that these sweets must have been specially bought for Fen to eat, and Fen took him out to play after eating one or two bites in a hurry, so there were so many left. Thinking of this, I didn't want to eat them anymore. But at the same time, I thought that these sweets were his, I loved him, and he loved me, so why not eat his sweets, and leave them for Fen to eat when she comes back? I insist on eating them, eating them all up, not leaving a single bite for Fen, so it was like kissing him, kissing the sweets one by one first, then eating them into my stomach, and then eating his heart!

Suddenly, I saw a bottle of rose juice wine on his table, and I remembered that he used to drink because I said I didn't love him. This time he is drinking again, he must still not be able to forget me, and Fen is loving him on the other hand, he has to relieve his sorrow with wine after being stimulated by contradictions. He said he hated me, he really hates me!

Xiang, you hate me, you don't know that I hate you even more! I said I don't love you anymore, I said we're just friends, even introducing Fen to you, it's not sincere, it's all testing you, and you're so honest, believing it's true. You hate me, but you don't know how regretful and resentful I am now...

Thinking of this regret, I can't help but want to drink and numb my own

Page 20

nerves... I know that the numbing power of alcohol is only temporary, and when I wake up from the alcohol, the sorrow and hatred will be even more profound, but I poured a full glass of his rose juice wine and drank it all in one gulp.

I haven't drunk alcohol for many years. After drinking this full glass today, I got drunk in a short time. Small golden flowers shot out in front of my eyes, and the floor was shaking. I couldn't help but feel terrified... What if they came back and saw me? In this drunken state? I hurriedly left a note to tell him and Fen that I came to see them, and staggered out of his house, returning to school.

On the road, the spring rain was falling in wisps. My heart was more sorrowful in my drunkenness. The cold wind blew, and I felt a chill. When I returned to school, I felt dizzy. I touched my bed and fell down, feeling very uncomfortable.

Thinking of today's encounter, my tears flowed down!

Biography of a Street Urchin (10)

—Made by Chen Jingsheng

This grass is really effective, victory is ours

Exploring the Plum Blossoms

—Qian Xu

Although the wind is very strong, it is always so warm when it blows on people; people are also lazy and don't want to do anything. All of this undoubtedly tells people that... "Spring has arrived."

Spring, how beautiful! The withered yellow grass has already taken off her haggard clothes, revealing a delicate face; the solemn expression no longer leaps on people's faces; the water in the pond or river is blown out by the spring breeze with poetic wrinkles... the birds on the branches sing tunes that have changed from sad to joyful; everything is filled with the breath of "life." Even though the waves of national economic depression are coming from every cheap big advertisement on the , they cannot wash away the plum blossoms, which have long been designated as our "national flower." At this time, they have sprung up in response to the season. Thus, the gentlemen and young masters who are generally idle and rich, because their "interest" has arrived, are making great "elegant" gestures of "exploring the plum blossoms."

We are born with a "fate" of being both busy and poor. Over the years, there has been no "year," no "festival," and no spring; we are surrounded by three-dimensional buildings all year round, only knowing to put on clothes when it is cold and take them off when it is hot. Several years have passed by in a muddle. However, this year, we finally got a very special opportunity to follow the gentlemen and young masters and also played once in the "grand event" of "exploring the plum blossoms" that is possessed by "idle" and "rich" people.

Because it seems that this little page can also occupy a place in my entire life history, I recorded it...

It was a clear morning, and when the gentle breeze blew past others and reached our side, we were a little intoxicated. Ah! This lovely nature.

Originally, having gotten used to a mechanical life, once able to throw ourselves into the arms of nature and enjoy the taste that we have always dreamed of, how eager and happy we were. The train was rushing forward with its head buried, occasionally emitting the whistling sound; the telephone poles on both sides retreated backwards in rows; the green fields, the dark farmers, the vendors singing tunes without rhythm, looked filled with the atmosphere of "life" in our joyful eyes.

Three hours of bumpy travel will not feel bitter in happiness. We finally stepped into the "Plum Garden" in Wuxi. Tens of thousands of plum trees were adorned with flowers, and the fragrance filled people's surroundings. We followed the other comrades—of course, the "plum blossom exploration" comrades—and ran around randomly. We climbed to the high places to look at the still waters of Taihu Lake in the same way. We looked at the noble and beautiful ladies in the crowd in the same way. Perhaps because of the "fate" of being born "busy and poor," we finally felt "bored." We discussed leaving, we wanted to return to Shanghai. Three hours of bumpy travel passed by in dejection, feeling both "long" and "bitter."

Eagerness and joy have become a thing of the past, and the atmosphere of "life" has also disappeared before our eyes. We understand that this kind of "elegant move" is ultimately a plaything for "idle" people, and is definitely not something that we, who are generally busy and poor, can do. What makes us tremble even more is the "economic depression" after the atmosphere of "life" has disappeared!

The harvest after a waste of spirit, time, and money is to make me patiently return to a lonely life and forever shatter the purple dream.

From Seeking Death to Scrambling for Life

—Meng Ruo

Sociologists say that suicide is also a kind of infectious disease. This is indeed true, as can be confirmed by the continuing occurrence of suicide incidents in Shanghai recently.

Is suicide meaningful or worthless? Courageous or cowardly? Worthy of sympathy or worthy of condemnation? I think it's hard to judge. It is human nature to cling to life and fear death. A person who goes down the road of suicide will not do so unless it is absolutely necessary. Therefore, people who commit suicide have their own reasons why they have to commit suicide, which cannot be easily praised or attacked by onlookers. No matter how complete the critic's reasons are, if you change places, I'm afraid you yourself will have some difficulty being in control, right? However, the impact of suicide on society is a bad phenomenon, and this is something that no one can deny.

Generally speaking, those who criticize suicide say in unison, "Humans are social animals, and they should take society as the premise and strive for society to be considered reasonable; but those who commit suicide do the opposite, thinking only of personal joys and sorrows, thus abandoning their due responsibility to society, and their actions are obviously wrong." But how many people who are social animals can reach this point? Let's say that suicide is a worthless, cowardly, and reprehensible act; we, who are still alive, can be regarded as meaningful, brave, and sympathetic people; but has society received any benefits from us? What have we contributed to society? How have we sacrificed and worked for society? Have we fulfilled our obligations to society? If we cannot provide satisfactory answers to these questions, then our words can at most be said to be temporary scrambling for life, and in fact, they have no significant meaning! Therefore, I say: rather than scrambling for life, it is better to seek death!

Lament

—Nier

Since the opening of the national film "Twin Sisters," for twenty days, everyone has praised it as wonderful. It is said (because the author was rejected twice by the "full house" sign, and dared not risk a third attempt due to the high cost of transportation) that Hu Die's crying, in particular, has won the audience's tears. Yesterday, Aunt Ningbo in the front building said to me: "Mr., "Twin Sisters" is really wonderful. It made my tears flow "dada"!"

Why is crying so deeply touching?

Speaking of crying, it reminds me of crying, and a bag of tears can't help but blur my eyes. So, I picked up a pen to write a lament. Fortunately, the Qingming Festival is approaching, so what's wrong with crying?

There is genuine crying and fake crying. If the crying in "Twin Sisters" (I sincerely regret not having heard it for myself) is fake crying. The viewers treat the fake as real, shedding a lot of tears along with it (as if it really happened), which is too unworthy. The day before yesterday, a man died next door. His wife wailed loudly at the coffin. This is genuine crying. The husband is called the sky. Having lost her sky, she can cry loudly. However, the onlookers come to listen to the crying, but take pleasure in other people's wailing, which is really incomprehensible! If the wife of the deceased knew the situation of the audience in "Twin Sisters," she would probably turn her crying into laughter, to the great joy of the mourners.

Besides genuine crying and fake crying, there is also crying that is both genuine and fake, neither genuine nor fake. If you have a mind for it, you can find it everywhere. However, writing aims to be popular, so let me give an example... An old comedian was famous for his crying at the time, and his monthly income was better than that of the mayor of Shanghai. But after he became a comedian, his later years were bleak. So, those who cry for people are also cried for by people. Don't see (should be hear) the sound of ah... from the radio, which makes people want to vomit. Those who cry take the old comedian as their ancestor, so those who cry for the old comedian are like a memorial offering condolences. However, it is both genuine and fake, neither genuine nor fake. The crying brings a steady stream of performances, which can also be said to be making the most of crying. If the old comedian has a spirit, has his crying reputation been swept away?

As for the hypocritical compassion of the cat crying for the mouse, what about after the death of a certain poet and a certain writer? This is crying, that is mourning. Poets and writers are not valued when they are alive, but become famous after death. I, Nier, am not smart, but I recommend it as a new technique for writers to ascend to the literary world. Is the author Zhang Jun interested?

Writing a lament alone, I don't realize where my tears are coming from. I originally wanted to cry again and again, but I was afraid that crying would hurt my spirit and affect my life, so I temporarily ended it, waiting for a continued crying.

After crying, I put down my pen and laughed three times, so that the income and expenditure are offset, so as to pay attention to hygiene.

Minor Problems

— Neil

Those of us who belong to the "tram class" and don't have cars to get around with, feel that copper coins are the most annoying things. Exchanging a double dime at the cigarette paper store yields forty-odd coins, which can be quite bothersome, especially in the summer. However, the tram fare (in the past) was forty coins. To avoid inexplicable losses, one has no choice but to dislike them.

I take the tram every day, and the inconvenience has become a habit. However, not long ago, all the passengers on the tram [gap] . It turned out that the double dime [gap] had dropped to forty-five coins, but the tram regulations had risen to forty-

Page 21

four coins. Even someone without [gap] arithmetical skills would know that the simple difference is only one copper coin [gap]. While saving the trouble of exchanging coins [continuation], the loss of only one [currency] coin is something one can still afford, so why not do it!

Now the market price of double dimes has returned to forty-eight coins, and passengers buying tickets with double dimes on the tram are no longer often seen. I believe this, like the lottery drawing for the aviation prize, is a minor issue like the evening newspaper raising its price. Because if the market price of double dimes were to drop to forty-three, or forty-two... coins, what would the tram company authorities do?

Amateur Mailbox

Dilemma

Editor:

I have a friend who is originally from Guangdong. In the 18th year of the Republic, he was visiting Shantou when an old woman was very pleased with my friend's personality and was willing to betroth her most beloved adopted daughter to him. Because the old woman had no children, only this adopted daughter, she loved her as the apple of her eye. She wanted my friend to become her live-in son-in-law. Later, my friend used three hundred silver dollars to marry her daughter (no conditions were stipulated at the time). Now they have a son who is three or four years old. However, my friend's parents in his hometown had already married him to a wife, and she has already given birth to a daughter. Before my friend married the old woman's daughter, they both knew that my friend already had a wife in his hometown. It is clear that their marriage was based on the wishes of both families. Now my friend wants to bring his wife back to his hometown to live with him because of the difficult life in Shantou, but both she and her mother are unwilling to return, putting my friend in an impossible situation. He wants to divorce her, but he can't bear to part with his son; if he reconciles with her, it would ultimately be futile. He is now in a dilemma and doesn't know what to do, so I am especially asking you, elder, to devise a good solution. I also hope you will answer the following questions in your amateur column:

(1) Is this kind of marriage legally valid?

(2) Who should the child born of this marriage belong to?

(3) How can the procedure for becoming a live-in son-in-law be established? Can such a live-in son-in-law without written documentation be legally established?

(4) Now my friend wants to deny being a live-in son-in-law and file a lawsuit in court. Is it possible for him to win back his son?

I humbly ask for answers to all of the above. I will be twelvefold grateful to you. I will repay your divine favor in the future.

Respectfully, Zhang Qiu

Answer: Bigamy is inherently unreasonable. Since Mr. Zhang's friend already had a wife in his hometown, he shouldn't have become someone else's live-in son-in-law. But the matter has already passed, so what's the point of talking about it. Now let's discuss what your friend should do?

From your letter, between the lines, it is vaguely seen that your friend and his Shantou wife have no love for each other. If your friend was deeply in love with his Shantou wife, then even if life were difficult, he would probably rather struggle under poverty and hunger than take a step back and think about returning to his hometown. Moreover, because they are unwilling to return, he wants to separate from them, and what he is reluctant to part with is only his "son." How could a person be so detached? From the woman's perspective, if she could truly trust him and empathize with his difficulties, then even if she returned to his hometown with him, despite the many inconveniences, she would definitely be willing to return with him. Therefore, based on this speculation, the editor dares to conclude that their love has broken down. Since the love between the two parties has broken down, then the editor believes that they should simply and quickly agree to separate without forcing each other to continue. But this is just the editor's opinion. Perhaps your friend has other hidden reasons, so this solution can only be provided for your friend's reference.

The four questions you asked are answered as follows:

(1) Legally invalid.

(2) Should be jointly owned by your friend and his wife.

(3) There are no specific conditions stipulated by law.

(4) The blood relationship between father and son and mother and son cannot be broken, and the mother must file a lawsuit to fight for it. The Editor

Novel

Lulu's Victory (10) (3)

— By Italian M. Serao, translated by Jing Xin

"One is here, the other is there," she murmured; "but what about before this? Enough! I must help."

"For so many powerful reasons, I cannot marry Robert Montelfranco." Finally, Lulu said to her mother.

"Your reasons are all extremely bizarre, my daughter," the mother replied, shaking her head.

"In short, I must frankly and clearly tell you that Robert does not please me, so I don't want to marry him."

"That's not frank at all; it's just a whim. Robert loves you."

"He will comfort himself."

"You have already exchanged marriage vows."

"We can cancel them. We are no longer living in the past when people could be forced into marriage."

"What about social criticism?"

"Mother, what is society?"

"People."

"Who is 'People' Mr.? I don't know him; I can't make myself unhappy because of 'People' Mr."

"You are a frightening daughter! But how can I talk to Robert? What can I say to him?"

"Say whatever you want. You are my mother. You should know what to do."

"Ah, indeed! Clean up the mess you've made. There will definitely be rumors."

"I don't think so; you can speak frankly and openly. Really, I think you can say bad things about me—call me arbitrary, frivolous, immature; just say I wouldn't make a good wife, I'm not serious at all, I lack dignity, and you should say my sister is—"

"Your sister? Have you lost your mind, Lulu!"

"Hush! It's easy for you to say that. Currently, Robert and Sophia are very cold to each other, but if they can get to know each other intimately, they can become close to each other, and then—who can say? If you marry off your eldest daughter first, people will praise you as a good mother."

"Indeed—"

"I won't go on like this without a husband... I'm just eighteen years old. I still want to make myself happy for a while; I still want to dance a lot... I want to spend my youth with my dear, kind little mother——"

"You are a little rascal," the mother replied, moved, embracing her daughter.

"We understand each other, right? Publicly spread this ugly news to Robert, but add that we must be friends forever, and we hope to see him often. If these two people love each other, they don't have to worry; it's destined."

Film Supplement

Mai Mulin on Greta Garbo (Part 2)

— Yuan Lin

Also, the climax of the story in the film is when she abdicates, but in reality, if her life were written into a true novel, it should probably be when she goes out to wander. At the same time, we also assume that her motivation for abdicating is love for a certain foreigner.

Apart from these deliberate errors, everything in the film can be said to be no different from history. I absolutely believe in Garbo's talent. This talent of hers can definitely show the extraordinary personality of Christine that she usually dreams of. In fact, she only decided to return from Europe after signing the contract to play this role.

This film is not a song and dance film, not a fairy tale, and not a work that simply shows off clothing to the audience. In other words, this does not belong to any work that has been successful in the past in film, drama, or even radio.

Recently, I have become a bit tired of those so-called dramatic films that are currently popular. I am very fond of great dramas, but only on the stage or in books. On the silver screen, which only emphasizes images and does not require beautiful writing, it instead causes aversion. In the near future, I am sure that these two arts (drama and film) will definitely become things with their own characteristics. The reason why I want to develop a continuous rhythm in my works that progresses according to the development of the story is precisely this.

Garbo is great! She has her talent! — No, besides talent, she has something else. When I watch her work, I feel like a strong vitality has suddenly been injected into a past character and started to move.

People probably know that Garbo doesn't like acting in front of people she doesn't know, but during filming, in addition to all the actors and directors, there are probably also the scriptwriters present, plus the electrical technicians, photographers, assistants, sound technicians, sound assistants, a female stage manager who records the director's words, and sometimes photographers who take stills for publicity, editors, etc., all walking around inside. The atmosphere of the film set is indeed too stimulating for sensitive actors. Therefore, for Garbo, a generally sensitive woman, it is indeed an unbearable thing to be surrounded by a large number of onlookers in addition to the people mentioned above. Because she has not had any stage experience.

But she is a very kind woman to the cameraman William Daniels, who has been working with us all along, and to the people we work with all the time. I always see her quietly talking to those temporary actresses. She is very fond of innocent children. She often gathers many children playing near her and personally invites them to eat Swedish snacks in front of the stove. I think these are the happiest times for her.

Garbo, who has lived in Europe for a long time, has become even more lonely than before. Since returning to America, she has only attended one screening of Marlene Dietrich's "Song of Love." Whatever her reasons, let us respect her silence and solitude! (End)

Film Review

Review of "General Yun"

— Luo Ping

"FRONTIERMARSHAL"

— Great Shanghai —

Among the monotonous heroic and beautiful "Western films," "General Yun" can be considered a better one.

Just as we are used to seeing childish fights in domestic films and have become extremely disgusted, we cannot help but be disgusted with the martial arts of the heroes in "Western films." The set of "General Yun" is just the same, the waste of American film production is truly appalling.

However, the depiction of the unscrupulous mayor in "General Yun" is very good.

That mayor, on the surface, is the highest local official responsible to the public under "democratic politics," but in reality, he is a bandit and assassin who sits on the ground and divides the spoils!

Naturally, such a mayor is a very good explanation of so-called democratic politics; however, the screenwriter of "General Yun" cannot help but have a shortcoming in his understanding. He can only see the corruption of this notorious mayor, but he cannot see that the essence of "democratic politics" is the trampling of the lower class by the upper social stratum.

The hero Wei Di, needless to say, is a generous and compassionate person who pities the weak. For example, he met Mary in the carriage to Johnston and fell in love with her. After learning that her father had been killed, he decided to stay in Johnston temporarily to protect her secretly. He is courageous, loyal, and loves to fight for justice. He personally visited Johnston to arrest Peng En, a huge bandit that the police did not dare to catch, and he insisted on going to catch him. When Warren vaguely told him some of the mayor's misdeeds, he tried his best to explore and punish this corrupt official. Thus, our hero moved Warren and even moved his former enemy Peng Si. Mary will definitely love him, and the girl Jing Qi in the tavern also loves him, even sacrificing her life for him.

Why did "General Yun" secretly write about the mayor being executed at the end and vigorously describe Jing Qi's sacrifice and the success of Wei Di and Mary's love? It is easy to understand that killing the evil corrupt official is ultimately very much related to "morality," and Jing Qi's death and Mary's (THROWS)

ERSELFINTOYATT'SARMS) are precisely the spoils of the hero's victory.

As for the descriptions of Warren and Peng En, "General Yun" only shows their brute force, loyalty, and worship of heroes. As for why they became bandits? How did their concepts of hero worship, loyalty, and brute force come about? No answers can be found in "General Yun."

This is what the screenwriter of "General Yun" would not understand; not only that, but more importantly, the current so-called "Western films" only see the heroes "flying on horseback on the pasture, shooting without fail," and "having a warm embrace and unwavering love," but do not see the vast number of farmers wailing in the midst of agricultural panic, and do not see these farmers realizing the ineffectiveness of agricultural relief laws under unbearable oppression and becoming aware of their own strength.

Nevertheless, the delicate style of "General Yun" ultimately broke the rough brushstrokes of Western films, such as (1) Wei Di and Warren enjoying wine together, (2) Jing Qi's death, (3) The triangular love between Wei Di, Mary, and Jing Qi is very successful, which is probably because the story itself is suitable for such a style.

The close and organic connection between the sound structure and the picture structure should be mentioned. For example, the scene of Wei Di catching thieves can very well express the atmosphere at that time. Among the actors, George O'Brien's Wei Di is of course very good at it. The roles of Mary, Warren, Jing Qi, and the mayor are also very hardworking.

However, the golden age of heroic and beautiful Western films has finally passed away. In China, "Fire Burning [Gap]" has been abandoned, and American martial arts films, which are not much better, are probably not welcome either. We are looking forward to a new film that is more in touch with the social reality of the American West.

Meeting Gift for Divorced Couples

— Reply

After a divorce, how should a couple meet when they reunite after a long separation? There is probably no set rule for this, right? Now I will describe a very interesting precedent. When you have a need, you can take it as a model.

Little Van Dyke returned to Hollywood from Europe. He and Joan Crawford are a couple who "amicably divorced," so when he arrived in Hollywood, Joan Crawford thought about going to the airport to meet him, but many Mingjiang held her back and wouldn't let her go. The reason is that she was afraid that this piece of news would be published in the newspaper, and everyone would misunderstand that she and Little Van Dyke would reunite. Now Joan and Franchot Tone (FRANCHOT LONE) are already in love and will soon announce their engagement. In this way, I am afraid that many rights and wrongs will be provoked again. Therefore, she did not go, but made a phone call to him, inviting him to her residence. He came. When they met, they shook hands happily, but did not kiss. Then Joan took her ex-husband's arm and inspected the various rooms of the house, pointing out many new pieces of furniture and decorations that had been newly placed after the separation. Little Van Dyke praised her intelligence one by one. Finally, they arrived in the sitting room. The two of them sat down and talked about everything non-domestic. At this time, Franchot Tone appeared. Did Little Van Dyke feel cramped? No! Not at all! The two of them actually talked happily. They talked about everything about the film set. They talked for two hours, completely ignoring Joan, and Joan watched the harmonious feelings of her two ex-husbands and future husband (note: not ex-husband and future husband) and enjoyed it.

Isn't this something that we Chinese people, who avoid seeing each other after a divorce, should emulate?

Prelude to "Under the Lamp Before the Moon"

The romantic blockbuster currently being screened in Nanjing stars the actress Elisa Landi. The background of the play is the famous gold-selling cave in the world, Monte Carlo, and the garden of Central Europe - Vienna. Its scenery is beautiful and unparalleled, needless to say.

In between, there are pursuits between men and women, and mutual stratagems of capture and release. The romantic parts are like drinking mellow wine, and the amorous parts are like playing with famous flowers. It is truly the essence of a love history. Elisa once revealed her charm in "Spring Colors of the Roman Palace." In this film, she plays a maid who learns to be a lady's maid, lively and charming, graceful and charming, and Paul Luga and others are also famous stars of the time. With so many big stars, a good background and an engaging plot, its beauty can be known. (Yet To Be Paid)

Film Novel

SCARLET EMPRESS (7)

— Su Mei

Catherine rode back on her horse, and Alexei greeted her. He whispered to her, "Not a moment has passed without me thinking of you. I must speak with you alone." Catherine looked at him coldly and said, "Be careful. Everyone's eyes are on us; they will tell my husband." Alexei said anxiously, "Tomorrow morning, when you go out riding, let's meet in the stables. No one will see us there—I'll arrange it." Catherine asked, "What if I don't ride tomorrow?" Alexei looked at her with pleading eyes and said, "You must go. No one will know."

Catherine returned to her room, and she seemed very happy while changing. Mary, who was helping her dress, saw this and asked, "Your Highness seems to be in high spirits now, is it to meet your husband?" Catherine laughed awkwardly, "Oh, I forgot I had a husband." Mary said playfully, "Then, Your Highness, I'm afraid you're going to meet your lover." Catherine said, "Mary, you are also a bad thing, do you also have a lover?" Mary said, "It would be good if I had a lover. Here, no one is without a lover. They all have them, except me." Catherine said, "I think our Empress probably doesn't have a lover." Mary said, "Huh, she doesn't? She has many lovers, changing them every month." After she finished speaking, she pleaded with Catherine, "You must not tell anyone that I said this. Otherwise, my tongue will be cut off." Catherine comforted her, "Don't worry, I won't tell anyone. I also don't believe your words. But I don't have a lover: I'm happy today because I'm going to see my mother." When Mary heard this, her face immediately changed. She said, "My Highness, don't you know?" Catherine asked, "Know what?" Mary said, "Your mother has already returned to Germany. She left last night at midnight! Her Majesty sent her back in the middle of the night."

Catherine suddenly felt lost, looking around and saying, "Why didn't she say she would see me?" After she finished speaking, she immediately went to find the Empress. At that time, the Empress was holding a state council meeting, and Catherine suddenly barged in. The Empress angrily scolded her for barging in without being summoned, but Catherine was not afraid at all, opening her eyes wide and asking, "Why did you send my mother away?" The Empress stood up and scolded, "Are you here to question me, you little rascal?" She said harshly to Catherine, "I sent your mother away because she didn't teach you well. I called you here to make you a good wife and to produce an heir for the Russian throne. Now get out of here immediately!" After she finished speaking, she rang the bell, and her favored bodyguard, Ivan Shuvalov, came in. She ordered him to send the Grand Duchess to her own palace. She said, "There, my own eyes can watch her! Teach her how to be a Russian wife!" (To be continued)
